25:T8e8f,<entryFree id="n16152" key="رَفَعَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">رَفَعَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Msb, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">رَفَعَ</orth>
                  </form>, (K, TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَفْعٌ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He raised it:</hi> [this is generally the best rendering, as it serves to indicate several particular significations which will be found explained in what follows:] <hi rend="ital">he elevated it; upraised it; uplifted it: he took it up: contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَفَضَهُ</foreign>: (Msb:) or <hi rend="ital">of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَضَعَهُ</foreign>: (S, Mgh, K:) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n16152-1" target="رفّعهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n16153"/></foreign>, (K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَرْفِيعٌ</foreign>; (TA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n16152-2" target="ارتفعهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (K;) for accord. to the “ Nawádir, ” you say, <foreign lang="ar">ارتفعهُ بِيَدِهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رَفَعَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he raised it, lifted it, heaved it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">took it up, with his hand</hi>]; but Az says that <foreign lang="ar">ارتفع</foreign> is intrans., and that he has heard no authority for its being trans., in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">رَفَعَ</foreign>, except that which he had read in the “ Nawádir el-Aaráb:” (TA:) <foreign lang="ar">رَفْعٌ</foreign> is sometimes applied to corporeal things, meaning the <hi rend="ital">raising,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">elevating,</hi> a thing <hi rend="ital">from the resting-place</hi> thereof: sometimes to a building, meaning the <hi rend="ital">rearing it, uprearing</hi> it, or <hi rend="ital">making</hi> it <hi rend="ital">high</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lofty:</hi> (Er-Rághib:) or in relation to corporeal things, it is used properly to denote motion, and removal: (Msb:) it signifies the <hi rend="ital">putting away or removing</hi> or <hi rend="ital">turning back</hi> a thing <hi rend="ital">after the coming</hi> or <hi rend="ital">arriving</hi> thereof; like as <foreign lang="ar">دَفْعٌ</foreign> signifies the putting away or removing or turning back a thing before the coming or arriving [thereof]: (Kull p. 185:) but in relation to ideal things, it is [tropically used, as it is also in many other cases, and] accorded in meaning to what the case requires. (Msb.) [In its principal senses, proper and tropical, <foreign lang="ar">رَفْعٌ</foreign> agrees with the Latin <hi rend="ital">Tollere.</hi>.] It is said in the Kur [ii. 60 and 87], <foreign lang="ar">رَفَعْنَا فَوْقَكُمُ ٱلطُّورَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">We raised above you from its resting-place the mountain:</hi> and in the same [xii. 2], <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُ ٱلَّذِى رَفَعَ السَّمٰوَاتِ بِغَيْرِ عَمَدٍ تَرَوْنَهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">God is He who raised the heavens without pillars that ye see;</hi> or, as <hi rend="ital">ye see them</hi>]: and in the same [ii. 121], <foreign lang="ar">وَإِذْ يَرْفَعُ إِبْرٰهِيمُ القَوَاعِدَ مِنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">البَيْتِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And when Abraham</hi>] <hi rend="ital">was rearing</hi> or <hi rend="ital">uprearing</hi> or <hi rend="ital">making high</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lofty</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the foundations of the House of God,</hi> at Mekkeh]. (Er-Rághib.) And you say, <foreign lang="ar">اِرْفَعْ هٰذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Take thou this:</hi> (Mgh:) or <hi rend="ital">take it and carry it</hi> [<hi rend="ital">away;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">take it up and remove it</hi>]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَفَعَ الزَّرعَ</foreign>, (Lh, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">رَفَعَهُ إِلَى البَيْدَرِ</foreign>, (Msb,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">رَفَعَ</orth>
                  </form>, (Lh,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَفْعٌ</foreign> (Lh, S) and <foreign lang="ar">رِفَاعَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رِفَاعٌ</foreign> [perhaps a mistranscription for <foreign lang="ar">رَفَاعُ</foreign>, which see below], (Lh, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He removed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">transported, the seed-produce from the place in which he had reaped it,</hi> (Lh,) or <hi rend="ital">carried it after the reaping,</hi> (S, K,) <hi rend="ital">to the place in which the grain was to be trodden out.</hi> (Lh, S, K.) [This last signification is said in the TA to be tropical; but according to a passage of the Msb quoted in the first sentence of this art., it is proper. In most of the phrases here following, the verb is undoubtedly used tropically.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَفَعُوا إِلَىَّ عُيُونَهُمْ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">They raised towards me their eyes</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلْتُ عَلَى فُلَانٍ فَلَمْ يَرْفَعْ بِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَأْسًا</foreign> (Mgh, TA *) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">I went in to such a one, and he did not look towards me, nor pay any regard,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">attention, to me.</hi> (Mgh.) [<foreign lang="ar">بِى</foreign> is not here a mistake for <foreign lang="ar">لِى</foreign>, for the phrase is often found thus written.]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رُفِعَ لِىَ الشَّىْءُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">The thing was, as it were, raised into view,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">it rose into view, to me;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">I saw the thing from afar.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَفَعَ السَّرَابُ الشَّخْصَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">رَفَعَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَفْعٌ</foreign>, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The mirage raised,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">elevated</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to the eye,</hi> (see an ex. near the end of the first paragraph of art. <foreign lang="ar">زول</foreign>)] <hi rend="ital">the figure of a man or some other thing seen from a distance;</hi> [or it may be allowable to render it, <hi rend="ital">made it to appear tall, and as though quivering, vibrating,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">playing up and down;</hi>] syn. <foreign lang="ar">زَهَاهُ</foreign> [of which, when it relates to the mirage, the meaning is best expressed by the latter of the two explanations here given]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَرَفَعْنَا بَعْضَهُمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَوْقَ بَعْضٍ دَرَجَاتٍ</foreign>, in the Kur [xliii. 31], means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">And we have exalted some of them above others in degrees of rank,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">station:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">نَرْفَعُ دَرَجَاتٍ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ نَشَآءُ</foreign>, in the same, [vi. 83, and xii. 76,] <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">We exalt in degrees of rank,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">station, whom We please:</hi> (Er-Rághib:) and <foreign lang="ar">وَٱللّٰهُ يَرْفَعُ مَنْ يَشَآءُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَيَخْفِضُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">And God exalteth whom He pleaseth, and abaseth:</hi> (S and TA:) and [in like manner,] <foreign lang="ar">رَفْعُ الذِّكْرِ</foreign> means the <hi rend="ital">exalting of one's fame;</hi> as in the Kur xciv. 4. (Er-Rághib.) But the words, <foreign lang="ar">وَإِلَى السَّمَآءِ كَيْفَ رُفِعَتْ</foreign>, in the Kur [lxxxviii. 18], indicate two meanings; <hi rend="ital">And to the heaven, how it is elevated in respect of its place;</hi> and <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">how it is exalted in respect of excellence, and exaltation of rank.</hi> (Er-Rághib.) [In like manner also,] <foreign lang="ar">فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللّٰهُ أَنْ تُرْفَعَ</foreign>, in the Kur [xxiv. 36], means <hi rend="ital">In houses which God hath permitted to be built;</hi> (Bd, TA;) accord. to some: (TA:) or, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">to be honoured;</hi> (Zj, Bd;) so says El-Hasan; (Zj;) or, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">to be exalted in estimation.</hi> (Er-Rághib.) It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهَ يَرْفَعُ العَدْلَ وَيَخْفِضُهُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Verily God exalteth the just, and maketh him to have the ascendency over the unjust, and</hi> at one time <hi rend="ital">abaseth him, so that He maketh the unjust to overcome him,</hi> in order to try his creatures, in the present world. (Az, TA.)                   <foreign lang="ar">أَنْفُسٍ</foreign>; <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">The pen</hi> of the recording angel <hi rend="ital">is withheld from three</hi> persons;] a saying of Mohammad, which means that nothing is recorded either for or against three persons; (Mgh, Msb; *) these three being the sleeper until he awakes, the afflicted with disease or the like, or the demented, until he recovers, and the child until he becomes big, or attains to puberty.
